# Learning Data Analytics Part 2: Extending and Applying Core Knowledge

> It’s one thing to work with data. It’s another to provide quality data sets and accurate visualizations for decisions to be made. If you are considering a course emphasis or a career in data analytics, this course can help you get off to a good start. Robin Hunt, CEO and co-founder of ThinkData Solutions, shares practical skills to help you get the most from your data and jumpstart your career in 

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge) | 3h 22m | Beginner | 22K learners

### 1. Working with Business Data

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Understanding business rules
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Growing up, I was pretty much the kid who followed the rules.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=4)** They were pretty much laid out for me.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=6)** I even have a typed copy of them from my mother's typewriter.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=9)** As a kid, I didn't always understand the rules right away, but I knew there would be consequences if I didn't follow them.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=17)** Rules of the business are no different.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=20)** I know that everything that I do with data is dictated by the rules of that business.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=25)** If I want to provide a list of top salespeople for a company, then I must know how they define top.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=32)** Is it revenue or is it number of orders?
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=36)** Documenting the rules until they're memorized is also great.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=40)** But having that documentation to mark up the changes of those rules over time can be super valuable from a historical perspective.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=48)** For example, if the business has changed systems, that's important to have a record of.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=54)** That way, I know that the systems are not combined with historical data and the current data that I have to work with, well, they're in two different datasets.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=63)** My documentation would include the points of time for the historical data, as well as the starting point for the new data in the new system.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=71)** You have likely heard me discuss the timing of data.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=74)** Part of the business rules may dictate the time of expected data.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=78)** Maybe you are forecasting sales data.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=80)** That means that there are orders and invoices.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=84)** Before it's an invoice, it must be an order in the system.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=88)** And well, knowing about the average length of time that an order converts to an invoice can support your forecasting.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=95)** There are business rules when a customer may even be considered a customer.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=99)** They may all be stored in the same customer table, but the rules may say that when a person first makes contact, they're considered a type of customer, like potential customer or lead, when they order something, that's when they become a real customer.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=114)** It could be that the business rules say that a customer is not a customer until they pay their invoice.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=120)** This rule helps us know how to use the customer table with the orders table to build a proper list of leads versus actual customers.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=129)** There are other types of business rules that require an action.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=132)** It might be that we have a rule that states if a customer hasn't ordered anything in 30 or 60 days that we send them we've missed you notices.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=142)** If we work in a regulated industry, we might be required to send notice after 30 days of a certain date.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=149)** These are all just examples of what I mean by rules.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=152)** Not following the rules does have a consequence.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=155)** If you don't remind customers that it's time to order, they may order too late, or they may not order at all.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=163)** And in a regulated industry where you're required to send notification, you might get deemed by a regulating body if you don't follow the rules.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=171)** Either way, strict or not strict, learn the rules and work with them in your data.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-business-rules?u=76281980&t=177)** The business rules are important because they not only help define the data, they drive what calculations you need, what timing matters, and they ultimately play a major role in all your queries, reporting and visualization.

#### Understanding noise in data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Imagine you just walked into a room full of people.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=3)** And everyone is talking about things that are really important.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=7)** You know that your response to that is to listen out to the most important information to you in all that noise.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=14)** Databases that support systems have a ton of data that we never need, but we have to deal with it, because it lives alongside the more meaningful data we do need.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=24)** If you Google noise and data, you'll hear a lot more about noise as it applies to different types of data and data requirements.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=32)** For the purposes of what we're learning at this stage, noise is just overall not meaningful information.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=38)** It's really not a part of our requirement, it's just information that gets in the way of the true sound of what we're trying to accomplish.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=46)** If you had used Excel data at all, you have likely deleted a column or two that you didn't need.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=52)** That's an example of removing noise.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=54)** The impact to leaving the noise in the data is that we're dealing with unnecessary fields in every data tool going forward.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=62)** We'll likely remove them later anyway to accomplish queries that may be total or aggregate data.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=69)** They make our file larger than necessary.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=71)** And overall, why process data on a machine that isn't needed anyway?
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=76)** And just like noise washes out true sound, too much unnecessary noise in your data washes out your ability to get to the point.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=84)** Let's take a look at a spreadsheet and spot the noise, and then deal with it.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=90)** For this example, we want to work with this file in and around invoices, customers, and orders.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=96)** We don't care about every single aspect that's been captured about the invoices, so we're going to remove some of the noise.

> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-noise-in-data?u=76281980&t=103)** All right, for example, I don't need the Delivery Method ID.

#### Breaking down the ask
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Soft skills are invaluable to an effective data analyst.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=4)** Being an active listener and a critical thinker is not just important, but it's mandatory.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=10)** You have to be able to break down what's being asked of you into workable requirements for you and the data.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=17)** In every data request or ask, I have some universal questions that I know that I will go through.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=23)** I'll confirm where the data is located.
>

>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=35)** I'll try to determine the key terms and definitions that the business uses.

>

>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=72)** Just remember, people have more details in their minds and they often don't communicate those details to you effectively up front.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/breaking-down-the-ask?u=76281980&t=79)** That's why it's important to ask the questions.

>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/challenge-getting-started?u=76281980&t=15)** You've been asked to provide a list of the top 50 customers based on their orders being the highest.

> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/challenge-getting-started?u=76281980&t=22)** What I want you to do is create a document that lists out the business roles based on this statement, top 50 customers based on their orders being the highest, and then also list out what you believe the potential noise in the data could be, and then list out your requirements to perform the ask.

#### Solution: Getting started
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=5)** - [Instructor] Now, it's important to remember that your information may vary from mine.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=10)** But if you got close or have some of the same types of information then you've done great on this challenge.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=16)** The goal was to provide the top 50 customers based on their order amounts.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=21)** And the business role that I determined was top customers based on the highest amount on any single order.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=28)** Now that could vary based on customer.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=30)** I also listed out the potential noise, like PickedByPersonID, and PickingCompletedWhen, and LastEditedBy information.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=39)** I also had some additional questions like, does back order matter for this report?
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=45)** And then also I listed out my certain requirements like, make a copy of the data, remove the noise, confirm that I don't have any duplicates, do a multisort, remove duplicates, sort by the highest dollar amount, filter for the top 50, and then copy it to a new sheet.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=64)** Again, these requirements could vary.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/solution-getting-started?u=76281980&t=66)** As long as you wrote out how you would start the process and the information you needed, then you did great on this challenge.

### 2. Building Data Sets with Queries

#### Understanding queries
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If you were to Google define the word query, you'll discover that a query is actually a question.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=7)** We have questions in data all the time, like how many X did we sell?
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=13)** That's an easy query, right?
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=16)** So yes, a query is a question.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=18)** But in regards to data analysis, it's also a statement created with a tool to answer a question with data.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=26)** You must identify where that information is stored, and how you will query it, using tools that query to produce the data for the answer.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=35)** This is why I refer to questions from leadership as ask, and refer to the action of querying data as a query or tool.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=45)** It's a lot to process, but queries really are nothing more than statements that you create that provide you the data that you need.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=52)** When we query data, it's a task to be completed with a tool.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=57)** The way you query in that tool is actually defined by the tool you're using.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=62)** And you're going to discover that the concepts are universal, but the points and clicks are definitely different based on the tool.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=70)** Remember that querying is also a process, and that one question can produce multiple queries or segments.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=78)** There are also different types of queries that you'll use throughout your data experience, and you'll use them based on what issues you're trying to solve and what you need to accomplish to get to the end goal of your task.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=90)** For most people at the beginning, it's just simple select queries powered by select statements.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=97)** These select queries are called select queries, because that's what they do, they select data from tables.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=104)** They're usually defined with just the fields you need to accomplish any given task.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=110)** This is just like manually removing the noise from the data that we talked about earlier.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=115)** But you're picking the fields that will help you answer the questions.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=119)** When you query with multiple tables involved, then you know from experience you have to address the joins and join types.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=126)** And in databases, these are still called select queries.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=129)** But in tools like Power Query, for example, you might hear them referred to as merge queries.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=135)** Then there are queries that you can leverage when you want to create data or copy data, or need to update data.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=143)** If you need to copy data from one table to another table, this type of query is called an append query.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=149)** If you need to update data, like changing X to Y, then you're doing what's called an update query.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=157)** You'll also need to know how to make a query distinct or unique.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=161)** This is a big time-saver, and sometimes it's an absolute must.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=165)** A distinct query looks at the fields you have selected, and then gives you a unique list.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=170)** It's important to note that a distinct or unique statement is more of a property of a select statement versus a type of query, like an update or a PIN.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=179)** Have you ever done an AutoSum in Excel?
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=182)** Well, we do the same things with queries.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=184)** These aggregate functions in queries are called total queries.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/understanding-queries?u=76281980&t=189)** Again, queries are so flexible, and when you learn your data and you know how to join it, and you understand the different types of queries that you might use, there is no data ask that you can't accomplish.

#### Building distinct queries

> **[7:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=467)** So it's okay for us to have orders without invoices.
>
> **[7:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=470)** However, it's not okay for us to have invoices without orders, because the first part of the process is the ordering process.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=478)** I'll go ahead and double-click the InvoicesWithoutOrders, and I get a perfect result, no records.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=486)** That means that every one of my invoices have an associated order, this is perfect.
>
> **[8:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=492)** And the Append query allowed me to take action by putting the missing records where they belong.
>
> **[8:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=499)** This scenario is not the only reason why you would use appends or even unions, but you can certainly see how easy it is to compile data together with Access as a tool.
>
> **[8:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=509)** Just remember these query types exist in all query tools.
>
> **[8:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=514)** Because this has meant to be educational, it's also pretty cookie cutter.
>
> **[8:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=517)** And well a life in data isn't always cookie cutter.
>
> **[8:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=521)** When you get ready to append data, one of the very first things you want to do is just double check that column headings and those data types, make sure they match.
>
> **[8:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-append-queries?u=76281980&t=529)** If they don't, then you guessed it, your first step before you Append is to clean them to match.

#### Challenge: Total number of orders by customer
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/challenge-total-number-of-orders-by-customer?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/challenge-total-number-of-orders-by-customer?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Here's our challenge.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/challenge-total-number-of-orders-by-customer?u=76281980&t=7)** We want to build a totals query that gives us a number of total orders placed by customer.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/challenge-total-number-of-orders-by-customer?u=76281980&t=13)** We also want it to be sorted with the highest number of orders first.
>

>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/ad-hoc-reporting?u=76281980&t=6)** These are the ones time requests from your leadership or manager, or sometimes even colleagues, reports like top customers or numbers of orders not invoiced or even forecasting are examples of ongoing reports that drive business decisions but ad hoc, I mean requests that aren't a standard part of your workload and they're requested informally sometimes by colleagues.

> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/ad-hoc-reporting?u=76281980&t=393)** Ad hoc requests when you have data skills is unavoidable.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/ad-hoc-reporting?u=76281980&t=397)** It's also important to remember your best practices because you never know when that ad hoc request is going to become the next big organizational report.

### 4. Pivot Data Anytime and Anywhere

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### What are pivots?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] To be able to pivot data is a fundamental skill of all data workers, not just analysts.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=5)** And really anyone that uses Excel with a dataset should be able to pivot.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=10)** For most people, it's hard to wrap your mind around how you can take a set of data and display it in a pivot format.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=17)** The displays are valuable and yes they can look very complex.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=20)** But what people don't realize is that it's actually harder to build the display without the tools dedicated to making pivot displays like PivotTables in Excel.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=29)** Just like the word query is a question and a tool, PivotTables are both a display and a tool.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=35)** PivotTables display values from data at the cross section of X and Y.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=39)** And when people think about X and Y they may start to think about their bad experiences with algebra in school.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=45)** And if you Google about the X and Y axis, you might say words like Cartesian coordinates system and you might just pass out.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=53)** Let's just keep it simple.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=58)** X is the main headings that go horizontal across the top of the pivot.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=62)** And the Y axis is the row headings that go vertical down the side of the pivot.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=67)** Now this will get more meaningful as we go through the rest of this chapter but where the X column headings and the Y row headings meet, well, that's the value.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=78)** Have you ever built a monthly budget?

> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=82)** This is the x-axis.

> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=113)** It will transform your data into a pivot display.

>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=129)** Looking at the pivot data file in her chapter folder, if I ask you to tell me for each month of the year for each customer, how much did we invoice them, you would certainly try to give me the answer and if you don't know how to pivot, you might start by some sorting.

> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-are-pivots?u=76281980&t=164)** Faced with the same request, and you do know how to use pivot tools, then it's as simple as adding the pivot on top of your data which we'll dig deeper into throughout this chapter.

#### Modifying pivots for readability
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/modifying-pivots-for-readability?u=76281980)

#### Building dashboards
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/building-dashboards?u=76281980)

### 7. Presenting Data in Meetings

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### Consider how to present data in meetings
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The most important piece of advice I can give on presenting data is this, don't forget that you know the data and your audience may not.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=9)** They haven't had the same amount of time with the data that you've had.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=13)** They haven't spent days validating and creating charts and pivot tables.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=17)** Remember, you're going to always need to prime them with a little information upfront Data that is being presented, especially in short bits of time, that's considered high volume or mission critical should always be include some primer information before any new piece of information is given.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=35)** If I'm about to show a key variable and how it impacts the information, but I didn't define how I got that variable, then I'm in trouble from the very start.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=45)** The whole time they should be thinking of what I'm telling them, they're instead going to be wondering, "How did get that variable because I've never seen it?"
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=54)** Not only will this distract from the presentation, but it'll also cause them to have questions that take away from the key points or even eat up the amount of time you have to go further.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=65)** Always include standard definitions of the data right up front.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=70)** For example, when I study children in K through 12, I create what's called cohorts, and I always define what I mean by cohort before I present any further information.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=82)** I clearly state how the children are defined into that cohort, the number of children or records that are in that cohort, and any other necessary definitions so they can go ahead and check that off in their brain.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=95)** That way they can focus on the insights I'm giving them about the data in the sample versus the questions I could have answered upfront.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=104)** Your studies will be different.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=106)** You might be defining the products that are included or even excluded from your data.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=111)** You may be talking about a different division or even a different department.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=115)** You might be talking about historical data or current data.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=118)** You might include time periods of focus.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=121)** But in any case, you should always define your data and the variables you're using.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=126)** I'm also very intentional to think over things that might help people to absorb the information at the pace I'm required to deliver it.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=133)** And whatever that is, it will be included.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=136)** It never hurts to run through your presentation with a peer or a colleague to give you clarity on what you may not realize needs explaining or defining because you already understand it.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=148)** And when I have the luxury of sending materials ahead to the audience, I can address some of those items in a simple document.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/consider-how-to-present-data-in-meetings?u=76281980&t=155)** I still highlight it again in the presentation, but then tell them to refer back to that information later as needed.

#### What to do before going company wide
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this course, we have talked about ad hoc reporting, those one time or one off requests that come to your desk.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=6)** However, there are times when you have reports or dashboards that will be consumed by the organization or by larger groups.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=13)** There are some key things to take into account when you're getting ready to go live within your organization.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=19)** You always want to identify your audience.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=22)** Who's actually going to be using the dashboards or reports?
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=26)** Is it internal people in the organization, like employees or executives?
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=30)** Or is it external, like customers or potential clients?
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=34)** Also, be sensitive to the branding guidelines.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=37)** Are there branding guidelines for externally-facing content?
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=41)** If you've never worked with the Marketing Department and you have no idea, here's your opportunity to explore this.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=47)** Internally, you might have executives who request everything fit a certain style standard.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=53)** For example, we support an organization that has requirements for everything that is around their brand.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=58)** From their email signature to their font usage.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=61)** We have a copy of those brand standards, and we follow it for the colors.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=66)** Fonts, logos, and everything we produce for them.
>

>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=76)** Who actually gets to access this data?
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=79)** And more importantly, who doesn't?
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=82)** Whether a group has access to the files or the dashboard, or even the PowerPoint version, you must make sure that everywhere the output lives, that only the appropriate people have permissions.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=94)** One way we support this particular effort is we have a SharePoint site that's dedicated to reporting.

>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=106)** It's an extra layer of permission, and it's worth it.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=109)** But that's just one example.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=110)** And again, you're controlled by the licenses that are given to everyone or not given to everyone in the organization.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=117)** So let's talk about that.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=119)** Every tool has licensing that controls what you can do with your published output or access to the files.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=126)** For example, you might want to share a report with a person who only wants to view the work.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=131)** But you have to ensure they have the right license to do that.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=135)** If they don't, then you can share that report with them all day and get nowhere.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=140)** You might want to leverage QR codes, but unless everyone has the minimum licensing requirement, it's a waste of time to provide that.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=148)** You may not be in control of the licensing for your organization, that's typically handled by the IT Department and the other decision-makers.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=156)** But you need to be able to communicate up front what constraints you face with the licensing that you do have.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=162)** This will allow the decision-makers to make a decision on the types of licenses that you might need, or that your organization needs.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=168)** Also, you will need to determine if any of the output needs to be emailed out, or if there's any other notification requirements.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=176)** An example would be that we have a paginated report, and this gets emailed out every day to the sales team.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=184)** Our notification is the fact that the email goes out with a report attached.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=189)** But we also have a dashboard, that due to the limitations of the data, it causes us to have to refresh the data every morning, so we have to notify everyone that the dashboard is refreshed.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=200)** Always consider the email and notification requirements of every report you build, and understand there's not a single answer every time.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=208)** You'll have to address it on a case-by-case basis.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=211)** Training guidance is so valuable, people don't naturally know how to use a dashboard to answer their own queries or questions.
>
> **[3:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=220)** Be sure to spend a little time building some training guidance on how to get the most out of the dashboard.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=225)** Minimum required training would be at least how to access the file dashboard or paginated report.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=232)** Who is the file meant for?
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=234)** Who is it meant to support?
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=235)** And what is the best use of the file, dashboard, or report?
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=239)** I would also include any key definitions that might support the consumer's understanding of the information.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/what-to-do-before-going-company-wide-10457637?u=76281980&t=245)** Until you have this simple checklist memorized, or so that you don't have to, I would recommend creating a checklist that contains all of these main areas, and be sure to include it at the beginning of every discussion for an organization-wide report, and maybe even every ad hoc request.

#### Leveraging PowerPoint for presentations
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/leveraging-powerpoint-for-presentations?u=76281980)

#### Continuing on with data analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] After going through the foundations and the application for data analysis, I often get asked, "What's next?"
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=6)** The first thing people tend to think about is which tools they should learn first.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=10)** "I should learn SQL, or Tableau, or even R."
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=14)** They're not wrong. Tools are important.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=17)** But I would argue if you're at the beginning of your career, you should focus on soft skills more than tools.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=22)** Data analysis is more than just learning points and clicks.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=26)** If you don't know why or how to critically look at something, you won't know what kind of questions to ask.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=32)** If you're not actively listening, you might miss things you otherwise wouldn't.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=36)** You can have the most beautiful statistical model in the world, but analysis is about how people use the information you give them, and that requires being able to communicate it effectively.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=47)** The only people that will be impressed with your fancy model are other analysts and not the people who need the information.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=54)** Explore the library for skills on active listening, critical thinking, and effective presentations of data.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=59)** These are very key components of an analyst.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=62)** Once you have those soft skills down, focus on specializing in an area.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=67)** If you enjoy data cleaning, mining, and querying, you might explore more on relational database design theory, as well as digging deeper into SQL and using it to query.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=78)** If you enjoyed the visualization portions of this course, you might explore the other tools dedicated to visualization, and dig deeper into tools like Power BI Desktop that we used in this course.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/learning-data-analytics-part-2-extending-and-applying-core-knowledge/continuing-on-with-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=88)** No matter what your next step will be, just keep making steps to further your understanding and your skills working with data.
